<p><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy&#39;s signature"><img alt="John F. Kennedy&#39;s signature" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg/150px-John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="35" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg/225px-John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg/300px-John_F_Kennedy_Signature_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="391" data-file-height="91" /></a><br />
<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/70px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="70" height="70" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/105px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg/140px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2424" data-file-height="2425" />
</p>
<a href="/wiki/List_of_personal_coats_of_arms_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of personal coats of arms of Presidents of the United States"><img alt="Coat of Arms of John F. Kennedy.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg/40px-Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="60" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg/60px-Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg/80px-Coat_of_Arms_of_John_F._Kennedy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="395" data-file-height="588" /></a></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;text-align:center;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:JFK_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:JFK series"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:JFK_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Template talk:JFK series"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:JFK_series&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>presidency of John F. Kennedy</b> began at noon <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EST</a> on January 20, 1961, when <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">Kennedy</a> was <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Inauguration of John F. Kennedy">inaugurated</a> as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the United States">35th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, and ended on November 22, 1963, upon his <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassination</a>, a span of 1,036 days. A <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> from <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, he took office following the <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">1960 presidential election</a>, in which he narrowly defeated <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>, the then–<a href="/wiki/Incumbent" title="Incumbent">incumbent</a> Vice President. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>.
</p><p>Kennedy's time in office was marked by <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> tensions with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. In Cuba, a failed attempt was made in April 1961 at the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs" title="Bay of Pigs">Bay of Pigs</a> to overthrow the government of <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a>. In October 1962, the Kennedy administration learned that Soviet <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missiles" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballistic missiles">ballistic missiles</a> had been deployed in Cuba; the resulting <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a> nearly resulted in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear war">nuclear war</a>, but ended when the Soviets withdrew the missiles. To contain Communist expansion in Asia, Kennedy increased the number of American military advisers in <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a> by a factor of 18; a further escalation of the American role in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> would take place after Kennedy's death. In <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, Kennedy's <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Progress" title="Alliance for Progress">Alliance for Progress</a> aimed to promote human rights and foster economic development.
</p><p>In domestic politics, Kennedy made bold proposals in his <a href="/wiki/New_Frontier" title="New Frontier">New Frontier</a> agenda, but many of his initiatives were blocked by the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_coalition" title="Conservative coalition">conservative coalition</a> of Northern Republicans and Southern Democrats. The failed initiatives include federal aid education, medical care for the aged, and aid to economically depressed areas. Though initially reluctant to pursue civil rights legislation, in 1963 Kennedy proposed a major civil rights bill that ultimately became the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Act_of_1964" title="Civil Rights Act of 1964">Civil Rights Act of 1964</a>. The economy experienced steady growth, low inflation and a drop in unemployment rates during Kennedy's tenure. Kennedy adopted <a href="/wiki/Keynesian_economics" title="Keynesian economics">Keynesian economics</a> and proposed a tax cut bill that was passed into law as the <a href="/wiki/Revenue_Act_of_1964" title="Revenue Act of 1964">Revenue Act of 1964</a>. Kennedy also established the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> and promised to land an American on the moon, thereby intensifying the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a> with the Soviet Union.
</p><p>Kennedy was <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">assassinated</a> in November 1963 while visiting <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, Texas. The <a href="/wiki/Warren_Commission" title="Warren Commission">Warren Commission</a> concluded that <a href="/wiki/Lee_Harvey_Oswald" title="Lee Harvey Oswald">Lee Harvey Oswald</a> acted alone in assassinating Kennedy, but the assassination gave rise to <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">a wide array of conspiracy theories</a>. Kennedy was the first <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> elected president, as well as the youngest candidate ever to win a U.S. presidential election. Historians and political scientists tend to <a href="/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States" title="Historical rankings of presidents of the United States">rank</a> Kennedy as an above-average president.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1960_election">1960 election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 1960 election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential election, 1960">United States presidential election, 1960</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1960.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ElectoralCollege1960.svg/230px-ElectoralCollege1960.svg.png" decoding="async" width="230" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ElectoralCollege1960.svg/345px-ElectoralCollege1960.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ElectoralCollege1960.svg/460px-ElectoralCollege1960.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1960.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1960 electoral vote results</div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy, who represented <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> from 1953 to 1960, had finished second on the vice presidential ballot of the <a href="/wiki/1956_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1956 Democratic National Convention">1956 Democratic National Convention</a>. After Republican President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Adlai_Stevenson_II" title="Adlai Stevenson II">Adlai Stevenson II</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1956_United_States_presidential_election" title="1956 United States presidential election">1956 presidential election</a>, Kennedy began to prepare a bid for the presidency in the <a href="/wiki/1960_United_States_presidential_election" title="1960 United States presidential election">1960 election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200612–13_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200612–13-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In January 1960, Kennedy formally announced his candidacy in that year's presidential election. Senator <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Humphrey" title="Hubert Humphrey">Hubert Humphrey</a> of Minnesota emerged as Kennedy's primary challenger in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Party (United States) presidential primaries, 1960">1960 Democratic primaries</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> but Kennedy's victory in the heavily-<a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> state of West Virginia prompted Humphrey's withdrawal from the race.<sup id="cite_ref-JFK-CE_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFK-CE-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1960_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1960 Democratic National Convention">1960 Democratic National Convention</a>, Kennedy fended off challenges from Stevenson and Senator <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> of Texas to win the presidential nomination on the first ballot of the convention.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy chose Johnson to be his vice-presidential running mate, despite opposition from many liberal delegates and Kennedy's own staff, including his brother <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy believed that Johnson's presence on the ticket would appeal to Southern voters, and he thought that Johnson could serve as a valuable liaison to the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200616–17-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Incumbent Vice President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> faced little opposition for the 1960 Republican nomination. He easily won the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_primaries,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party presidential primaries, 1960">party's primaries</a> and received the nearly-unanimous backing of the delegates at the <a href="/wiki/1960_Republican_National_Convention" title="1960 Republican National Convention">1960 Republican National Convention</a>. Nixon chose <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Cabot Lodge, Jr.">Henry Cabot Lodge, Jr.</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations" title="United States Ambassador to the United Nations">chief U.S. delegate to the United Nations</a>, as his running mate.<sup id="cite_ref-JFK-CE_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFK-CE-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Both presidential nominees traveled extensively during the course of the campaign. Not wanting to concede any state as "unwinnable," Nixon undertook a <a href="/wiki/Fifty-state_strategy" title="Fifty-state strategy">fifty-state strategy</a>, while Kennedy focused the states with the most <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral</a> votes.<sup id="cite_ref-JFK-CE_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFK-CE-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Ideologically, Kennedy and Nixon agreed on the continuation of the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> <a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">containment</a> policy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200617_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200617-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Major issues in the campaign included the economy, Kennedy's <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and whether the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> space and missile programs had surpassed those of the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199315_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199315-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 8, 1960, Kennedy defeated Nixon in one of the closest presidential elections of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDudleyShiraev200883_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDudleyShiraev200883-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy won the popular vote by a narrow margin of 120,000 votes out of a record 68.8 million ballots cast.<sup id="cite_ref-JFK-CE_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFK-CE-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He won the electoral vote by a wider margin, receiving 303 votes to Nixon's 219. 14 <a href="/wiki/Unpledged_elector" title="Unpledged elector">unpledged electors</a><sup id="cite_ref-Unpledged_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unpledged-9">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> from two states—<a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Alabama,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential election in Alabama, 1960">Alabama</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Mississippi,_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="United States presidential election in Mississippi, 1960">Mississippi</a>—voted for Senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_F._Byrd" title="Harry F. Byrd">Harry F. Byrd</a> of Virginia, as did one <a href="/wiki/Faithless_elector" title="Faithless elector">faithless elector</a><sup id="cite_ref-Faithless_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faithless-11">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_elections_in_Oklahoma" title="United States presidential elections in Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDudleyShiraev200883_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDudleyShiraev200883-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In the concurrent congressional elections, Democrats retained wide majorities in both the House of Representatives and the Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996441_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996441-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy was the first person born in the 20th century to be elected president,<sup id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1961_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1961-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and, at age 43, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States_by_age" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of the United States by age">youngest person</a> elected to the office.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199321_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199321-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Roosevelt_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roosevelt-16">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> He was also the first <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> elected to the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Inauguration">Inauguration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Inauguration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Inauguration_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Inauguration of John F. Kennedy">Inauguration of John F. Kennedy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jfk_inauguration.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Jfk_inauguration.jpg/210px-Jfk_inauguration.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Jfk_inauguration.jpg/315px-Jfk_inauguration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Jfk_inauguration.jpg/420px-Jfk_inauguration.jpg 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="552" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jfk_inauguration.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">Chief Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren" title="Earl Warren">Earl Warren</a> administers the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Oath of office of the President of the United States">presidential oath of office</a> to John F. Kennedy at <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">the Capitol</a>, January 20, 1961.</div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy was inaugurated as the nation's 35th president on January 20, 1961, on the East Portico of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">United States Capitol</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States" title="Chief Justice of the United States">Chief Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren" title="Earl Warren">Earl Warren</a> administered the <a href="/wiki/Oath_of_office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Oath of office of the President of the United States">oath of office</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In his inaugural address, Kennedy spoke of the need for all Americans to be active citizens, famously saying: "Ask not what your country can do for you; ask what you can do for your country." He also invited the nations of the world to join together to fight what he called the "common enemies of man: tyranny, poverty, disease, and war itself."<sup id="cite_ref-JFKlibrary.org_Inaugural_Address_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKlibrary.org_Inaugural_Address-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> To these admonitions he added:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>All this will not be finished in the first one hundred days. Nor will it be finished in the first one thousand days, nor in the life of this Administration, nor even perhaps in our lifetime on this planet. But let us begin." In closing, he expanded on his desire for greater internationalism: "Finally, whether you are citizens of America or citizens of the world, ask of us here the same high standards of strength and sacrifice which we ask of you.<sup id="cite_ref-JFKlibrary.org_Inaugural_Address_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JFKlibrary.org_Inaugural_Address-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The address reflected Kennedy's confidence that his administration would chart an historically significant course in both domestic policy and foreign affairs. The contrast between this optimistic vision and the pressures of managing daily political realities at home and abroad would be one of the main tensions running through the early years of his administration.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKempe201152_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKempe201152-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/John_F._Kennedy%27s_Inaugural_Address" class="extiw" title="s:John F. Kennedy&#39;s Inaugural Address">Full text</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource has information on &quot;John F. Kennedy&#39;s Inaugural Address&quot;"><img alt="Wikisource has information on &quot;John F. Kennedy&#39;s Inaugural Address&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/11px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="12" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/17px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/22px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></a>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox" style="width:auto;text-align:left;line-height:1.2em;margin-left:1em; margin-right:0; float:right; clear:right;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="3" style="line-height:1.5em;font-size:110%;background:#DCDCDC;text-align:center">The Kennedy Cabinet</th></tr><tr><th>Office</th><th>Name</th><th>Term</th></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#000"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold">John F. Kennedy</th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">Secretary of State</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Dean_Rusk" title="Dean Rusk">Dean Rusk</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">Secretary of Treasury</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/C._Douglas_Dillon" title="C. Douglas Dillon">C. Douglas Dillon</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Robert_McNamara" title="Robert McNamara">Robert McNamara</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">Attorney General</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Postmaster_General" title="United States Postmaster General">Postmaster General</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/J._Edward_Day" title="J. Edward Day">J. Edward Day</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr class="mw-empty-elt"></tr><tr><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/John_A._Gronouski" title="John A. Gronouski">John A. Gronouski</a></th><td>1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Interior" title="United States Secretary of the Interior">Secretary of the Interior</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Stewart_Udall" title="Stewart Udall">Stewart Udall</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Agriculture" title="United States Secretary of Agriculture">Secretary of Agriculture</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Orville_Freeman" title="Orville Freeman">Orville Freeman</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Commerce" title="United States Secretary of Commerce">Secretary of Commerce</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Luther_H._Hodges" title="Luther H. Hodges">Luther H. Hodges</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Labor" title="United States Secretary of Labor">Secretary of Labor</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Goldberg" title="Arthur Goldberg">Arthur Goldberg</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1962</td></tr><tr class="mw-empty-elt"></tr><tr><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/W._Willard_Wirtz" title="W. Willard Wirtz">W. Willard Wirtz</a></th><td>1962&#8211;1963</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="background:#D1D1D1"></td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Health,_Education,_and_Welfare" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Secretary of Health, Education, and Welfare">Secretary of Health,<br />Education, and Welfare</a></td><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Abraham_A._Ribicoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Abraham A. Ribicoff">Abraham A. Ribicoff</a></th><td>1961&#8211;1962</td></tr><tr class="mw-empty-elt"></tr><tr><th style="font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Anthony_J._Celebrezze" title="Anthony J. Celebrezze">Anthony J. Celebrezze</a></th><td>1962&#8211;1963</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Kennedy spent the eight weeks following his election choosing his cabinet, staff and top officials.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He retained <a href="/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover" title="J. Edgar Hoover">J. Edgar Hoover</a> as <a href="/wiki/Director_of_the_Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Director of the Federal Bureau of Investigation">Director of the Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allen_Dulles" title="Allen Dulles">Allen Dulles</a> as <a href="/wiki/Director_of_Central_Intelligence" title="Director of Central Intelligence">Director of Central Intelligence</a>. <a href="/wiki/C._Douglas_Dillon" title="C. Douglas Dillon">C. Douglas Dillon</a>, a business-oriented Republican who had served as Eisenhower's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Under_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Under Secretary of State">Undersecretary of State</a>, was selected as Secretary of the Treasury. Kennedy balanced the appointment of the relatively conservative Dillon by selecting liberal Democrats to hold two other important economic advisory posts; <a href="/wiki/David_E._Bell" title="David E. Bell">David E. Bell</a> became the Director of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">Bureau of the Budget</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Walter_Heller" title="Walter Heller">Walter Heller</a> served as the Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Economic_Advisers" title="Council of Economic Advisers">Council of Economic Advisers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200620–21_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200620–21-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Robert_McNamara" title="Robert McNamara">Robert McNamara</a>, who was well known as one of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Whiz_Kids_(Ford)" title="Whiz Kids (Ford)">Whiz Kids</a>", was appointed Secretary of Defense. Rejecting liberal pressure to choose Stevenson as Secretary of State, Kennedy instead turned to <a href="/wiki/Dean_Rusk" title="Dean Rusk">Dean Rusk</a>, a restrained former <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Truman</a> official, to lead the Department of State. Stevenson accepted a non-policy role as the ambassador to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200620–21_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200620–21-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In spite of concerns over <a href="/wiki/Nepotism" title="Nepotism">nepotism</a>, Kennedy's father insisted that <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy" title="Robert F. Kennedy">Robert F. Kennedy</a> become Attorney General, and the younger Kennedy became the "assistant president" who advised on all major issues.<sup id="cite_ref-asstpresident_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asstpresident-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> McNamara and Dillon also emerged as important advisers from the cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200637_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200637-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg/210px-President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg/315px-President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg/420px-President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6017" data-file-height="4668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_John_F._Kennedy_with_His_White_House_Staff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President John F. Kennedy (seated) with members of his White House staff</div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy scrapped the decision-making structure of Eisenhower,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199322_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199322-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> preferring an organizational structure of a wheel with all the spokes leading to the president; he was ready and willing to make the increased number of quick decisions required in such an environment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199323,_25_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199323,_25-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Though the cabinet remained an important body, Kennedy generally relied more on his staffers within the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" title="Executive Office of the President of the United States">Executive Office of the President</a>. Unlike Eisenhower, Kennedy did not have a <a href="/wiki/White_House_Chief_of_Staff" title="White House Chief of Staff">chief of staff</a>, but instead relied on a small number of senior aides, including appointments secretary <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_O%27Donnell" title="Kenneth O&#39;Donnell">Kenneth O'Donnell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200631–32,_35_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200631–32,_35-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Advisor_(United_States)" title="National Security Advisor (United States)">National Security Advisor</a> <a href="/wiki/McGeorge_Bundy" title="McGeorge Bundy">McGeorge Bundy</a> was the most important adviser on foreign policy, eclipsing Secretary of State Rusk.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200635–37_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200635–37-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ted_Sorensen" title="Ted Sorensen">Ted Sorensen</a> was a key advisor on domestic issues who also wrote many of Kennedy's speeches.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201255_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201255-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Other important advisers and staffers included <a href="/wiki/Larry_O%27Brien" title="Larry O&#39;Brien">Larry O'Brien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_M._Schlesinger_Jr." title="Arthur M. Schlesinger Jr.">Arthur M. Schlesinger Jr.</a>, press secretary <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Salinger" title="Pierre Salinger">Pierre Salinger</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_D._Taylor" title="Maxwell D. Taylor">Maxwell D. Taylor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/W._Averell_Harriman" title="W. Averell Harriman">W. Averell Harriman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996459_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996459-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200632–33,_64,_69_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200632–33,_64,_69-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy maintained cordial relations with Vice President Johnson, who was involved in issues like civil rights and space policy, but Johnson did not emerge as an especially influential vice president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200641–43_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200641–43-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_appointments">Judicial appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Judicial appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_Supreme_Court_candidates" title="John F. Kennedy Supreme Court candidates">John F. Kennedy Supreme Court candidates</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_judges_appointed_by_John_F._Kennedy" title="List of federal judges appointed by John F. Kennedy">List of federal judges appointed by John F. Kennedy</a></div>
<p>Kennedy made two appointments to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a>. After the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Evans_Whittaker" title="Charles Evans Whittaker">Charles Evans Whittaker</a> in early 1962, President Kennedy assigned Attorney General Kennedy to conduct a search of potential successors, and the attorney general compiled a list consisting of Deputy Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Byron_White" title="Byron White">Byron White</a>, Secretary of Labor <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Goldberg" title="Arthur Goldberg">Arthur Goldberg</a>, federal appellate judge <a href="/wiki/William_H._Hastie" title="William H. Hastie">William H. Hastie</a>, legal professor <a href="/wiki/Paul_A._Freund" title="Paul A. Freund">Paul A. Freund</a>, and two state supreme court justices. Kennedy narrowed his choice down to Goldberg and White, and he ultimately chose the latter, who was quickly confirmed by the Senate. A second vacancy arose later in 1962 due to the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Felix_Frankfurter" title="Felix Frankfurter">Felix Frankfurter</a>. Kennedy quickly appointed Goldberg, who easily won confirmation by the Senate. Goldberg resigned from the court in 1965 to accept appointment as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations" title="United States Ambassador to the United Nations">ambassador to the United Nations</a>, but White remained on the court until 1993, often serving as a key swing vote between liberal and conservative justices.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Due in part to the creation of new federal judgeships in 1961, Kennedy appointed 130 individuals to the federal courts. Among his appointments was <a href="/wiki/Thurgood_Marshall" title="Thurgood Marshall">Thurgood Marshall</a>, who later joined the Supreme Court.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200644–45_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200644–45-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs">Foreign affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_John_F._Kennedy_administration" title="Foreign policy of the John F. Kennedy administration">Foreign policy of the John F. Kennedy administration</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Cold_War_and_flexible_response">The Cold War and flexible response</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Cold War and flexible response">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Flexible_response" title="Flexible response">Flexible response</a></div>
<p>Kennedy's foreign policy was dominated by American confrontations with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, manifested by proxy contests in the global state of tension known as the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Like his predecessors, Kennedy adopted the policy of <a href="/wiki/Containment" title="Containment">containment</a>, which sought to stop the spread of Communism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704–705_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704–705-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> President Eisenhower's <a href="/wiki/New_Look_(policy)" title="New Look (policy)">New Look</a> policy had emphasized the use of nuclear weapons to <a href="/wiki/Deterrence_theory" title="Deterrence theory">deter</a> the threat of Soviet aggression. Fearful of the possibility of a global nuclear war, Kennedy implemented a new strategy known as <a href="/wiki/Flexible_response" title="Flexible response">flexible response</a>. This strategy relied on conventional arms to achieve limited goals. As part of this policy, Kennedy expanded the <a href="/wiki/United_States_special_operations_forces" title="United States special operations forces">United States special operations forces</a>, elite military units that could fight unconventionally in various conflicts. Kennedy hoped that the flexible response strategy would allow the U.S. to counter Soviet influence without resorting to war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201276–77_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201276–77-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, he ordered a massive build-up of the nuclear arsenal to establish superiority over the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704–705_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008704–705-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In pursuing this military build-up, Kennedy shifted away from Eisenhower's deep concern for budget deficits caused by military spending.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996489–490_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996489–490-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to Eisenhower’s warning about the perils of the military-industrial complex, Kennedy focused on rearmament. From 1961 to 1964 the number of nuclear weapons increased by 50 percent, as did the number of B-52 bombers to deliver them. The new ICBM force grew from 63 intercontinental ballistic missiles to 424. He authorized 23 new Polaris submarines, each of which carried 16 nuclear missiles. Meanwhile, he called on cities to prepare fallout shelters for nuclear war.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_and_the_Soviet_Union">Cuba and the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cuba and the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bay of Pigs Invasion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Pigs_Invasion" title="Bay of Pigs Invasion">Bay of Pigs Invasion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg/210px-President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg/315px-President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg/420px-President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="607" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Kennedy_and_Vice_President_Johnson_prior_to_ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Kennedy and Vice President Johnson take a leisurely stroll on the White House grounds.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fulgencio_Batista" title="Fulgencio Batista">Fulgencio Batista</a>, a Cuban dictator friendly towards the United States, had been forced out office in 1959 by the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Revolution" title="Cuban Revolution">Cuban Revolution</a>. Many in the United States, including Kennedy himself, had initially hoped that Batista's successor, <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">Fidel Castro</a> would preside over democratic reforms. Dashing those hopes, by the end of 1960 Castro had embraced <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>, confiscated American property, and accepted Soviet aid.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200650–51_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200650–51-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The Eisenhower administration had created a plan to overthrow Castro's regime though an invasion of Cuba by a counter-revolutionary insurgency composed of U.S.-trained, anti-Castro Cuban exiles<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002233,_238_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002233,_238-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> led by <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a> paramilitary officers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199369–73_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199369–73-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy had campaigned on a hard-line stance against Castro, and when presented with the plan that had been developed under the Eisenhower administration, he enthusiastically adopted it regardless of the risk inflaming tensions with the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-fiftyyearslater_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiftyyearslater-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Some advisors, including Schlesinger, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Under_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Under Secretary of State">Under Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Chester_Bowles" title="Chester Bowles">Chester Bowles</a>, and former Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Dean_Acheson" title="Dean Acheson">Dean Acheson</a>, opposed the operation, but Bundy and McNamara both favored it, as did the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>, despite serious reservations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200652–55_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200652–55-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 17, 1961, Kennedy ordered the Bay of Pigs Invasion: 1,500 American-trained Cubans, called <a href="/wiki/Brigade_2506" title="Brigade 2506">Brigade 2506</a>, landed on the inlet of that name.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199371,_673_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199371,_673-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The goal was to spark a widespread popular uprising against Castro, but no such uprising occurred. <sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201268–69_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201268–69-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Although the Eisenhower administration plan had called for an American airstrikes to hold back the Cuban Counter attack until the invaders were established, Kennedy rejected the strike because it would emphasize the American sponsorship of the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996493–495_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996493–495-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> CIA director Allen Dulles later stated that they thought the president would authorize any action required for success once the troops were on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199371,_673_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199371,_673-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> By April 19, 1961, the Cuban government had captured or killed the invading exiles, and Kennedy was forced to negotiate for the release of the 1,189 survivors. After twenty months, Cuba released the captured exiles in exchange for a ransom of $53&#160;million worth of food and medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002268–294,_838–839_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002268–294,_838–839-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the lack of direct U.S. military involvement, the Soviet Union, Cuba, and the international community all recognized that the U.S. had backed the invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996493–495_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996493–495-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy focused primarily on the political repercussions of the plan rather than military considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves199395–97_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves199395–97-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath, he took full responsibility for the failure, saying: "We got a big kick in the leg and we deserved it. But maybe we'll learn something from it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002290,_295_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002290,_295-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's approval ratings climbed afterwards, helped in part by the vocal support given to him by Nixon and Eisenhower.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2003370–371_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2003370–371-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Outside the United States, however, the operation undermined Kennedy's reputation as a world leader, and raised tensions with the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201270–71_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201270–71-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Kennedy administration <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">banned all Cuban imports</a>, convinced the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> to expel Cuba, and turned to the CIA to plot the overthrow of Castro through its <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Project" title="Cuban Project">Cuban Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008707–708_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008707–708-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A secret review conducted by Lyman Kirkpatrick of the CIA concluded that the failure of the invasion resulted less from a decision against airstrikes and had more to do with the fact that Cuba had a much larger defending force and that the operation suffered from "poor planning, organization, staffing and management".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2003363–366_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2003363–366-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy dismissed Dulles as director of the CIA and increasingly relied on close advisers like Sorensen, Bundy, and Robert Kennedy as opposed to the Joint Chiefs of Staff, the CIA, and the State Department.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200664–65,_68_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200664–65,_68-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vienna_Summit_and_the_Berlin_Wall">Vienna Summit and the Berlin Wall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Vienna Summit and the Berlin Wall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Kennedy,_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/210px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/315px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg/420px-John_Kennedy%2C_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="590" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Kennedy,_Nikita_Khrushchev_1961.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy meeting with <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Premier" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Premier">Soviet Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in June, 1961</div></div></div>
