data-height=&quot;360&quot; data-bandwidth=&quot;538384&quot; data-framerate=&quot;24&quot;/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;"><img alt="File:President Kennedy in Vienna, 1961, USIA.ogv" style="width:220px;height:165px" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/President_Kennedy_in_Vienna%2C_1961%2C_USIA.ogv/220px--President_Kennedy_in_Vienna%2C_1961%2C_USIA.ogv.jpg" /><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/President_Kennedy_in_Vienna%2C_1961%2C_USIA.ogv" title="Play media" target="new"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Kennedy_in_Vienna,_1961,_USIA.ogv" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/U.S._Information_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Information Agency">U.S. Information Agency</a> motion picture on the 1961 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Summit" class="mw-redirect" title="Vienna Summit">Vienna Summit</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the Bay of Pigs invasion, Kennedy announced that he would meet with Soviet Premier <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> at the June 1961 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_summit" title="Vienna summit">Vienna summit</a>. The summit would cover several topics, but both leaders knew that the most contentious issue would be that of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, which had been divided into two cities with the start of the Cold War. The enclave of <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> lay within Soviet-allied <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, but was supported by the U.S. and other Western powers. The Soviets wanted to reunify Berlin under the control of East Germany, partly due to the large number of East Germans who had fled to West Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201274,_77–78_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201274,_77–78-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Khrushchev had clashed with Eisenhower over the issue but had tabled it after the <a href="/wiki/1960_U-2_incident" title="1960 U-2 incident">1960 U-2 incident</a>; with the inauguration of a new U.S. president, Khrushchev was once again determined to bring the status of West Berlin to the fore. Kennedy's handling of the Bay of Pigs crisis convinced him that Kennedy would wither under pressure. Kennedy, meanwhile, wanted to meet with Khrushchev as soon as possible in order to reduce tensions and minimize the risk of nuclear war. Prior to summit, Harriman advised Kennedy, "[Khrushchev's] style will be to attack you and see if he can get away with it. Laugh about it, don't get into a fight. Rise above it. Have some fun."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200672–73,_76_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200672–73,_76-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 4, 1961, the president <a href="/wiki/Vienna_summit" title="Vienna summit">met with Khrushchev in Vienna</a>, where he made it clear that any treaty between <a href="/wiki/East_Berlin" title="East Berlin">East Berlin</a> and the Soviet Union that interfered with U.S. access rights in West Berlin would be regarded as an act of war.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993161–175_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993161–175-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The two leaders also discussed the situation in Laos, the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a>, China's <a href="/wiki/China_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="China and weapons of mass destruction">fledgling nuclear program</a>, a potential nuclear test ban treaty, and other issues.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200678–79_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200678–79-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after Kennedy returned home, the Soviet Union announced its intention to sign a treaty with East Berlin that would threaten Western access to West Berlin. Kennedy, depressed and angry, assumed that his only option was to prepare the country for nuclear war, which he personally thought had a one-in-five chance of occurring.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993161–175_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993161–175-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the weeks immediately after the Vienna summit, more than 20,000 people fled from East Berlin to the western sector in reaction to statements from the USSR. Kennedy began intensive meetings on the Berlin issue, where Dean Acheson took the lead in recommending a military buildup alongside NATO allies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993185_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993185-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In a July 1961 speech, Kennedy announced his decision to add $3.25&#160;billion to the defense budget, along with over 200,000 additional troops, stating that an attack on West Berlin would be taken as an attack on the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993201_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993201-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Soviet Union and East Berlin began blocking further passage of East Berliners into West Berlin and erected barbed wire fences across the city, which were quickly upgraded to the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993213_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993213-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy acquiesced to the wall, though he sent Vice President Johnson to West Berlin to reaffirm U.S. commitment to the enclave's defense. In the following months, in a sign of rising Cold War tensions, both the U.S. and the Soviet Union ended a moratorium on nuclear weapon testing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200685–86_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200685–86-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuban_Missile_Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cuban Missile Crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a></div>
<p>In the aftermath of the Bay of Pigs and invasion Cuban and Soviet leaders feared that the United States was planning another invasion of Cuba, and Khrushchev increased economic and military assistance to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006203–205_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006203–205-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Kennedy administration viewed the growing <a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Soviet_Union_relations" title="Cuba–Soviet Union relations">Cuba-Soviet alliance</a> with alarm, fearing that it could eventually pose a threat to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012113–114_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012113–114-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy did not believe that the Soviet Union would risk placing nuclear weapons in Cuba, but he dispatched CIA <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_U-2" title="Lockheed U-2">U-2</a> spy planes to determine the extent of the Soviet military build-up.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012113–114_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012113–114-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On October 14, 1962, the spy planes took photographs of intermediate-range ballistic missile sites being built in Cuba by the Soviets. The photos were shown to Kennedy on October 16, and a consensus was reached that the missiles were offensive in nature.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993345_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993345-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the Vienna Summit, Khrushchev came to believe that Kennedy would not respond effectively to provocations. He saw the deployment of the missiles in Cuba as a way to close the "<a href="/wiki/Missile_gap" title="Missile gap">missile gap</a>" and provide for the defense of Cuba. By late 1962, both the United States and the Soviet Union possessed <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_ballistic_missile" title="Intercontinental ballistic missile">intercontinental ballistic missiles</a> (ICBMs) capable of delivering nuclear payloads, but the U.S. maintained well over 100 ICBMs, as well as over 100 <a href="/wiki/Submarine-launched_ballistic_missile" title="Submarine-launched ballistic missile">submarine-launched ballistic missile</a> (SLBMs). By contrast, the Soviet Union did not possess SLBMs, and had less than 25 ICBMs. The placement of missiles in Cuba thus threatened to significantly enhance the Soviet Union's <a href="/wiki/First_strike_capability" class="mw-redirect" title="First strike capability">first strike capability</a> and even the nuclear imbalance.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006205–208_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006205–208-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy himself did not believe that the deployment of missiles to Cuba fundamentally altered the strategic balance of the nuclear forces; more significant for him was the political and psychological implications of allowing the Soviet Union to maintain nuclear weapons in Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006211_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006211-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg" title="File:John F Kennedy Address on the Buildup of Arms in Cuba.ogg">Address on the Buildup of Arms in Cuba</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_2" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="1056.3485034014" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="John_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/John_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (38 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="37761" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/a/a9/John_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg/John_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="104672" /><track src="https://commons.wikimedia.org/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3AJohn_F_Kennedy_Address_on_the_Buildup_of_Arms_in_Cuba.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=srt&amp;origin=%2A" kind="subtitles" type="text/x-srt" srclang="en" label="English (en) subtitles" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Kennedy addressing the nation on October 22, 1962, about the buildup of arms on Cuba</div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Kennedy faced a dilemma: if the U.S. attacked the sites, it might lead to nuclear war with the U.S.S.R., but if the U.S. did nothing, it would appear weak. On a personal level, Kennedy needed to show resolve in reaction to Khrushchev, especially after the Vienna summit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993245_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993245-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> To deal with the crisis, he formed an ad hoc body of key advisers, later known as <a href="/wiki/EXCOMM" title="EXCOMM">EXCOMM</a>, that met secretly between October 16 and October 28.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006207–208_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006207–208-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The members of EXCOMM agreed that the missiles must be removed from Cuba, but differed as to the best method. Some favored an airstrike, possibly followed by an invasion of Cuba, but Robert Kennedy and others argued that a surprise airstrike would be immoral and would invite Soviet reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006211–212_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006211–212-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The other major option that emerged was a naval blockade, designed to prevent further arms shipments to Cuba. Though he had initially favored an immediate air strike, the president quickly came to favor the naval blockade the first method of response, while retaining the option of an airstrike at a later date.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006210,_212–213_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006210,_212–213-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> EXCOMM voted 11-to-6 in favor of the naval blockade, which was also supported by British ambassador <a href="/wiki/David_Ormsby-Gore,_5th_Baron_Harlech" title="David Ormsby-Gore, 5th Baron Harlech">David Ormsby-Gore</a> and Eisenhower, both of whom were consulted privately.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006215–217_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006215–217-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On October 22, after privately informing the cabinet and leading members of Congress about the situation, Kennedy announced on national television that the U.S. had discovered evidence of the Soviet deployment of missiles to Cuba. He called for the immediate withdrawal of the missiles, as well as the convening of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> and the Organization of American States (OAS). Finally, he announced that the U.S. would begin a naval blockade of Cuba in order to intercept arms shipments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006217–218_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006217–218-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 23, in a unanimous vote, the OAS approved a resolution that endorsed the blockade and called for the removal of the Soviet nuclear weapons from Cuba. That same day, Stevenson presented the U.S. case to the UN Security Council, though the Soviet Union's <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_veto_power" title="United Nations Security Council veto power">veto power</a> precluded the possibility of passing a Security Council resolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006219_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006219-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On the morning of October 24, over 150 U.S. ships were deployed to enforce the blockade against Cuba. Several Soviet ships approached the blockade line, but they stopped or reverse course to avoid the blockade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006220_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006220-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On October 25, Khrushchev offered to remove the missiles if the U.S. promised not to invade Cuba. The next day, he sent a second message in which he also demanded the removal of <a href="/wiki/PGM-19_Jupiter" title="PGM-19 Jupiter">Jupiter missiles</a> from <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008721–722_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008721–722-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> EXCOMM settled on what has been termed the "<a href="/wiki/Trollope_ploy" title="Trollope ploy">Trollope ploy</a>;" the U.S. would respond to the Khrushchev's first message and ignore the second. On October 27, Kennedy sent a letter to Khrushchev calling for the removal of the Cuban missiles in return for an end to the blockade and an American promise to refrain from invading Cuba. At the president's direction, Robert Kennedy privately informed the Soviet ambassador that the U.S. would remove the missiles from Turkey after the end of the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006225–226_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006225–226-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Few members of EXCOMM expected Khrushchev to agree to the offer, but on October 28 Khrushchev publicly announced that he would withdraw the missiles from Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006225–226_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006225–226-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Negotiations over the details of the withdrawal continued, but the U.S. ended the naval blockade on November 20, and most Soviet soldiers left Cuba by early 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006228_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006228-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. publicly promised never to invade Cuba and privately agreed to remove its missiles in Italy and Turkey; the missiles were by then obsolete and had been supplanted by submarines equipped with <a href="/wiki/UGM-27_Polaris" title="UGM-27 Polaris">UGM-27 Polaris</a> missiles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKenney2000184–186_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKenney2000184–186-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath of the crisis, the United States and the Soviet Union established a <a href="/wiki/Moscow%E2%80%93Washington_hotline" title="Moscow–Washington hotline">hotline</a> to ensure clear communications between the leaders of the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008723_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008723-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The Cuban Missile Crisis brought the world closer to nuclear war than at any point before or since. In the end, "the humanity" of the two men prevailed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKenney2000189_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKenney2000189-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The crisis improved the image of American willpower and the president's credibility. Kennedy's approval rating increased from 66% to 77% immediately thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993425_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993425-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's handling of the Cuban Missile Crisis has received wide praise from many scholars, although some critics fault the Kennedy administration for precipitating the crisis with its efforts to remove Castro.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012124–126_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley2012124–126-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008722–723_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008722–723-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Khrushchev, meanwhile, was widely mocked for his performance, and was removed from power in October 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996506_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996506-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_Test_Ban_Treaty">Nuclear Test Ban Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Nuclear Test Ban Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Partial_Nuclear_Test_Ban_Treaty" title="Partial Nuclear Test Ban Treaty">Partial Nuclear Test Ban Treaty</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/American_University_speech" title="American University speech">American University speech</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10,_1963.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg/210px-President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg/315px-President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg/420px-President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10%2C_1963.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2632" data-file-height="2562" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Kennedy_American_University_Commencement_Address_June_10,_1963.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy delivers the <a href="/wiki/Commencement_speech" title="Commencement speech">commencement speech</a> at <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a>, June 10, 1963.</div></div></div>
<p>Troubled by the long-term dangers of <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination" title="Radioactive contamination">radioactive contamination</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">nuclear weapons proliferation</a>, Kennedy and Khrushchev agreed to negotiate a nuclear test ban treaty, originally conceived in Adlai Stevenson's 1956 presidential campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993552_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993552-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In their Vienna summit meeting in June 1961, Khrushchev and Kennedy had reached an informal understanding against nuclear testing, but further negotiations were derailed by the resumption of nuclear testing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993227_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993227-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Soviet-American relations improved after the resolution of the Cuban Missile Crisis, and the powers resumed negotiations over a test ban treaty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230–231_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230–231-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Jfk_American_University_4654_06-10-63.ogg" title="File:Jfk American University 4654 06-10-63.ogg"><i>World Peace</i> Speech</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_3" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="1606.8391609977" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Jfk_American_University_4654_06-10-63.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/b/b5/Jfk_American_University_4654_06-10-63.ogg/Jfk_American_University_4654_06-10-63.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="121544" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Jfk_American_University_4654_06-10-63.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (130 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="129753" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Speech from <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> by John F. Kennedy, June 10, 1963 (duration 26:47)</div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>On June 10, 1963, Kennedy delivered a <a href="/wiki/Commencement_address" class="mw-redirect" title="Commencement address">commencement address</a> at the <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> in Washington, D.C., in which he announced that the Soviet had agreed to resume nuclear test ban treaty talks. He and also announced, for the purpose of showing "good faith and solemn convictions", his decision to postpone planned atmospheric nuclear weapons tests, and pledged that the U.S. would refrain from conducting further tests as long as all other nations would do the same.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993514_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993514-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The U.S., Kennedy commented, was seeking a goal of "complete disarmament" of nuclear weapons, and he vowed that America "will never start a war".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The following month, Kennedy sent W. Averell Harriman to Moscow to negotiate a test-ban treaty with the Soviets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993542_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993542-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Each party sought a comprehensive test ban treaty, but a dispute over the number of on-site inspections allowed in each year prevented a total ban on testing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230–231_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230–231-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Ultimately, the United States, the United Kingdom, and the Soviet Union agreed to a limited treaty that prohibited atomic testing on the ground, in the atmosphere, or underwater, but not underground.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993550_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993550-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The treaty represented an important deescalation of Cold War tensions, but both countries continued to build their respective nuclear stockpiles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006232–234_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006232–234-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. and the Soviet Union also reached an agreement whereby the U.S. sold millions of bushels of wheat to the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006230-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Southeast Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg/210px-John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg/315px-John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg/420px-John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_and_Harold_Holt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy with <a href="/wiki/Harold_Holt" title="Harold Holt">Harold Holt</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Treasurer_of_Australia" title="Treasurer of Australia">Treasurer of Australia</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Office" title="Oval Office">Oval Office</a> in 1963</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Laos">Laos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Laos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>When briefing Kennedy, Eisenhower emphasized that the communist threat in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> required priority. Eisenhower considered <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> to be "the cork in the bottle;" if it fell to Communism, Eisenhower believed other Southeast Asian would, as well.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParmet1983133-37_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParmet1983133-37-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The Joint Chiefs proposed sending 60,000 American  soldiers to uphold the friendly government, but Kennedy rejected this strategy in the aftermath of the failed Bay of Pigs invasion. He instead sought a negotiated solution between the government and the left-wing insurgents, who were backed by <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a> and the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008708_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008708-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy was unwilling to send more than a token force to neighboring <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, a key American ally. By the end of the year, Harriman had helped arrange the <a href="/wiki/International_Agreement_on_the_Neutrality_of_Laos" title="International Agreement on the Neutrality of Laos">International Agreement on the Neutrality of Laos</a>, which temporarily brought an end to the crisis, but the <a href="/wiki/Laotian_Civil_War" title="Laotian Civil War">Laotian Civil War</a> continued.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200696–98_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200696–98-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Though he was unwilling to commit U.S. forces to a major military intervention in Laos, Kennedy did approve <a href="/wiki/CIA_activities_in_Laos" title="CIA activities in Laos">CIA activities in Laos</a> designed to defeat Communist insurgents through bombing raids and the recruitment of the <a href="/wiki/Hmong_people" title="Hmong people">Hmong people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996498_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996498-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Role_of_the_United_States_in_the_Vietnam_War" title="Role of the United States in the Vietnam War">Role of the United States in the Vietnam War</a></div>
<p>During his presidency, Kennedy continued policies that provided political, economic, and military support to the <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnamese</a> government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunniganNofi1999257_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunniganNofi1999257-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Vietnam had been divided into a communist North Vietnam and a non-Communist South Vietnam after the <a href="/wiki/1954_Geneva_Conference" title="1954 Geneva Conference">1954 Geneva Conference</a>, but North Vietnamese leader <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a> in 1960 to foment support for unification in South Vietnam. The president of South Vietnam, <a href="/wiki/Ngo_Dinh_Diem" title="Ngo Dinh Diem">Ngo Dinh Diem</a>, had alienated many of his constituents by avoiding land reforms, refusing to hold free elections, and staging an anti-Communist purge. Kennedy escalated American involvement in Vietnam in 1961 by financing the South Vietnam army, increasing the number of U.S. military advisers above the levels of the Eisenhower administration, and authorizing U.S. helicopter units to provide support to South Vietnamese forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006256–261_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006256–261-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Though Kennedy provided support for South Vietnam throughout his tenure, Vietnam remained a secondary issue for the Kennedy administration until 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006256–257_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006256–257-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy increasingly soured on Diem, whose violent <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_crisis" title="Buddhist crisis">crackdown on Buddhist practices</a> further galvanized opposition to his leadership. In August 1963, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cabot_Lodge,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Cabot Lodge, Jr.">Henry Cabot Lodge, Jr.</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Nolting" title="Frederick Nolting">Frederick Nolting</a> as the U.S. ambassador to South Vietnam. Days after his arrival in South Vietnam, Lodge reported that several South Vietnamese generals sought the assent of the U.S. government to their plan of removing Diem from power. The Kennedy administration was split regarding not just the removal of Diem, but also their assessment of the military situation in South Vietnam and the proper U.S. role in the country. Without the full support of the U.S., General <a href="/wiki/D%C6%B0%C6%A1ng_V%C4%83n_Minh" title="Dương Văn Minh">Dương Văn Minh</a> (known as "Big Minh") called off the potential coup in South Vietnam. Big Minh again approached the U.S. about a coup, and administration official informed him that the U.S. would neither support or oppose the toppling of Diem. In November 1963, a junta of senior military officers <a href="/wiki/1963_South_Vietnamese_coup" title="1963 South Vietnamese coup">executed Diem</a> and his influential brother, <a href="/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Nhu" title="Ngô Đình Nhu">Ngô Đình Nhu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006262–268_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006262–268-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By November 1963, there were 16,000 American military personnel in South Vietnam, up from Eisenhower's 900 advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In the aftermath of the aborted coup in September 1963, the Kennedy administration reevaluated its policies in South Vietnam. Kennedy rejected both the full-scale deployment of ground soldiers, but also rejected the total withdrawal of U.S. forces from the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006265–266_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006265–266-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Historians disagree on whether the U.S. military presence in Vietnam would have escalated had Kennedy survived and been re-elected in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Fueling the debate are statements made by Secretary of Defense McNamara in the film "<a href="/wiki/The_Fog_of_War" title="The Fog of War">The Fog of War</a>" that Kennedy was strongly considering pulling out of Vietnam after the 1964 election.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The film also contains a tape recording of Lyndon Johnson stating that Kennedy was planning to withdraw, a position that Johnson disagreed with.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlightLang2005276_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlightLang2005276-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy had signed National Security Action Memorandum (NSAM) 263, dated October 11, which ordered the withdrawal of 1,000 military personnel by the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-NSAM_263_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSAM_263-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallek2003680_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallek2003680-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Such an action would have been a policy reversal, but Kennedy was moving in a less hawkish direction since his acclaimed speech about world peace at <a href="/wiki/American_University" title="American University">American University</a> on June 10, 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-AmUniv_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmUniv-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_America">Latin America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Latin America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_and_Latin_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennedy and Latin America">Kennedy and Latin America</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alessandri-Kennedy(2).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG/210px-Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="210" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG/315px-Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG/420px-Alessandri-Kennedy%282%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="982" data-file-height="663" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alessandri-Kennedy(2).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy with Chilean President <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Alessandri" title="Jorge Alessandri">Jorge Alessandri</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy sought to contain the threat of communism in Latin America by establishing the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Progress" title="Alliance for Progress">Alliance for Progress</a>, which sent aid to some countries and sought greater <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> standards in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002788,_789_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2002788,_789-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The Alliance for Progress drew from the <a href="/wiki/Good_Neighbor_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Good Neighbor Policy">Good Neighbor Policy</a> in its peaceful engagement with Latin America, and from the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> in its expansion of aid and economic relationships. Kennedy also emphasized close personal relations with Latin American leaders, frequently hosting them in the White House.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008716–717_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008716–717-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Information_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Information Agency">U.S. Information Agency</a> was given an important role of reaching out to Latin Americans in Spanish, Portuguese, and French media.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The goals of the Alliance for Progress included long-term permanent improvement in living conditions through the advancement of industrialization, the improvement of communications systems, the reduction of trade barriers, and an increase in the number and diversity of exports from Latin America. At a theoretical level, Kennedy’s planners hoped to reverse the under-development of the region and its dependency on North America. Part of the administration's motivation was the fear that Castro’s Cuba would introduce anti-American political and economic changes if development did not take place.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The U.S. also continued to use covert means in order to reduce Soviet influence. When Kennedy took office, the CIA had begun formulating plans for the assassination of <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Trujillo" title="Rafael Trujillo">Rafael Trujillo</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>. Kennedy privately instructed the CIA that any such planning must include plausible deniability by the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReeves1993140–142_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReeves1993140–142-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The administration had no role in Trujillo's assassination in 1961, but supported the government of Trujillo's successor, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bosch_(politician)" title="Juan Bosch (politician)">Juan Bosch</a>. The United States launched a covert intervention in <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a> to deny the left-wing leader <a href="/wiki/Cheddi_Jagan" title="Cheddi Jagan">Cheddi Jagan</a> power in an independent Guyana, and forced a reluctant Britain to participate.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The CIA also engaged in operations in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> against left-wing leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008717–718_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008717–718-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_East">Middle East</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Middle East">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq">Iraq</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Iraq">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran,_1961.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg/210px-Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg/315px-Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg/420px-Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran%2C_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="991" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy_with_Shah_of_Iran,_1961.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iran's <a href="/wiki/Shah" title="Shah">Shah</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Reza_Pahlavi" title="Mohammad Reza Pahlavi">Mohammad Reza Pahlavi</a>, Kennedy, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">U.S. Defense Secretary</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_McNamara" title="Robert McNamara">Robert McNamara</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Room_(White_House)" title="Cabinet Room (White House)">White House Cabinet Room</a> on April 13, 1962</div></div></div>
<p>Relations between the United States and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> became strained following the <a href="/wiki/14_July_Revolution" title="14 July Revolution">overthrow of the Iraqi monarchy</a> on July 14, 1958, which resulted in the declaration of a republican government led by Brigadier <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Karim_Qasim" title="Abd al-Karim Qasim">Abd al-Karim Qasim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson20153-5_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson20153-5-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On June 25, 1961, Qasim mobilized troops along the border between Iraq and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, declaring the latter nation "an indivisible part of Iraq" and causing a short-lived "Kuwait Crisis". The United Kingdom—which had just granted Kuwait independence on June 19, and whose economy was heavily dependent on Kuwaiti oil—responded on July 1 by dispatching 5,000 troops to the country to deter an Iraqi invasion. At the same time, Kennedy dispatched a U.S. Navy task force to <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, and the U.K. (at the urging of the Kennedy administration) brought the dispute to United Nations Security Council, where the proposed resolution was vetoed by the Soviet Union. The situation was resolved in October, when the British troops were withdrawn and replaced by a 4,000-strong <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> force.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson201536_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson201536-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1961, Qasim's government passed Public Law 80, which restricted the British- and American-owned <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Petroleum_Company" title="Iraq Petroleum Company">Iraq Petroleum Company</a> (IPC)'s <a href="/wiki/Concession_(contract)" title="Concession (contract)">concessionary holding</a> to those areas in which oil was actually being produced, effectively expropriating 99.5% of the IPC concession. U.S. officials were alarmed by the expropriation as well as the recent Soviet veto of an Egyptian-sponsored UN resolution requesting the admittance of Kuwait as UN member state, which they believed to be connected. Senior National Security Council adviser <a href="/wiki/Robert_Komer" title="Robert Komer">Robert Komer</a> worried that if the IPC ceased production in response, Qasim might "grab Kuwait" (thus achieving a "stranglehold" on Middle Eastern oil production), or "throw himself into Russian arms." Komer also made note of widespread rumors that a nationalist coup against Qasim could be imminent, and had the potential to "get Iraq back on [a] more neutral keel."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson201537,_40-42_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson201537,_40-42-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The anti-imperialist and anti-communist <a href="/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Iraq_Region" title="Arab Socialist Ba&#39;ath Party – Iraq Region">Iraqi Ba'ath Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Ramadan_Revolution" title="Ramadan Revolution">overthrew and executed Qasim in a violent coup</a> on February 8, 1963. While there have been persistent rumors that the CIA orchestrated the coup, declassified documents and the testimony of former CIA officers indicate that there was no direct American involvement, although the CIA was actively seeking a suitable replacement for Qasim within the Iraqi military and had been informed of an earlier Ba'athist coup plot.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson201545,_57-58_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson201545,_57-58-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> The Kennedy administration was pleased with the outcome and ultimately approved a $55 million arms deal for Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibson201560-61,_80_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibson201560-61,_80-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Israel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg/170px-Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg/255px-Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg/340px-Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1824" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kennedy-Golda_Meir.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy with <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs_Minister_of_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Affairs Minister of Israel">Israeli Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Golda_Meir" title="Golda Meir">Golda Meir</a>, December 27, 1962</div></div></div>
<p>President Kennedy ended the arms embargo that the Eisenhower and Truman administrations had enforced on <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> in favor of increased security ties, becoming the founder of the <a href="/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_military_relations" title="Israel–United States military relations">U.S.-Israeli military alliance</a>. Describing the protection of Israel as a moral and national commitment, he was the first to introduce the concept of a 'special relationship' between the U.S. and Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In 1962, the Kennedy administration sold Israel a major weapon system, the <a href="/wiki/MIM-23_Hawk" title="MIM-23 Hawk">Hawk antiaircraft missile</a>. Historians differ as to whether Kennedy pursued security ties with Israel primarily to shore up support with Jewish-American voters, or because of his admiration of the Jewish state.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kennedy warned the Israeli government against the production of nuclear materials in <a href="/wiki/Dimona" title="Dimona">Dimona</a>, which he believed could instigate a nuclear arms-race in the Middle East. After the existence of a nuclear plant was initially denied by the Israeli government, <a href="/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion" title="David Ben-Gurion">David Ben-Gurion</a> stated in a speech to the Israeli <a href="/wiki/Knesset" title="Knesset">Knesset</a> on December 21, 1960, that the purpose of the nuclear plant at <a href="/wiki/Beersheba" title="Beersheba">Beersheba</a> was for "research in problems of arid zones and desert flora and fauna."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalt2008201_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalt2008201-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> When Ben-Gurion met with Kennedy in New York, he claimed that Dimona was being developed to provide nuclear power for desalinization and other peaceful purposes "for the time being."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalt2008201_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalt2008201-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In 1962, the US and Israeli governments agreed to an annual inspection regime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalt2008202_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalt2008202-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Despite these inspection, <a href="/wiki/Rodger_Davies" title="Rodger Davies">Rodger Davies</a>, the director of the State Department's Office of Near Eastern Affairs, concluded in March 1965 that Israel was developing <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a>. He reported that Israel's target date for achieving nuclear capability was 1968–1969.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESalt2008203_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESalt2008203-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_and_developing_countries">Decolonization and developing countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Decolonization and developing countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana,_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_(JFKWHP-AR6409-B).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg/210px-President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg/315px-President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg/420px-President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana%2C_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_%28JFKWHP-AR6409-B%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="787" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_John_F._Kennedy_Meets_with_the_President_of_the_Republic_of_Ghana,_Osagyefo_Dr._Kwame_Nkrumah_(JFKWHP-AR6409-B).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy with <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a>, the first president of an independent <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, March 1961</div></div></div>
<p>Between 1960 and 1963, twenty-four <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_by_date_of_formation" title="List of sovereign states by date of formation">countries</a> gained independence as the process of <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> continued. Many of these nations sought to avoid close alignment with either the United States or the Soviet Union, and in 1961, the leaders of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Kennedy set out to woo the leaders and people of the Third World, expanding economic aid and appointing knowledgeable ambassadors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008711–712_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008711–712-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> His administration established the <a href="/wiki/Food_for_Peace" title="Food for Peace">Food for Peace</a> program and the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> to provide aid to developing countries in various ways. The Food for Peace program became a central element in American foreign policy, and eventually helped many countries to develop their economies and become commercial import customers.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having chaired a subcommittee on Africa of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, Kennedy had developed a special interest in Africa. During the election campaign, Kennedy managed to mention Africa nearly 500 times, often attacking the Eisenhower administration for losing ground on that continent.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy considered the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Crisis" title="Congo Crisis">Congo Crisis</a> to be one of the most important foreign policy issues facing his presidency, and he supported a UN operation that prevented the secession of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Katanga" title="State of Katanga">State of Katanga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006239–242_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006239–242-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>  Kennedy also sought closer relations with Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">Jawaharlal Nehru</a> through increased economic and a tilt away from <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, but made little progress in bringing India closer to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008712–713_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008712–713-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy hoped to minimize Soviet influence in Egypt through good relations with President <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">Gamal Abdel Nasser</a>, but Nasser's <a href="/wiki/Arab_Cold_War" title="Arab Cold War">hostility</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> closed off the possibility of closer relations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2008713–714_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2008713–714-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In Southeast Asia, Kennedy helped mediate the <a href="/wiki/West_New_Guinea_dispute" title="West New Guinea dispute">West New Guinea dispute</a>, convincing Indonesia and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> to agree to <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Free_Choice" title="Act of Free Choice">a plebiscite</a> to determine the status of <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_New_Guinea" title="Netherlands New Guinea">Dutch New Guinea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006254–255_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006254–255-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_international_trips">List of international trips</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: List of international trips">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Kennedy made eight international trips during his presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_affairs">Domestic affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Domestic affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Frontier">New Frontier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: New Frontier">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami,_Florida_(10998767613).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg/210px-John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg/315px-John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg/420px-John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami%2C_Florida_%2810998767613%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="473" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_F._Kennedy_shaking_hands_in_Miami,_Florida_(10998767613).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kennedy in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, Florida, November 18, 1963</div></div></div>
<p>Kennedy called his domestic program the "<a href="/wiki/New_Frontier" title="New Frontier">New Frontier</a>"; it included initiatives such as medical care for the elderly, federal aid to education, and the creation of a department of housing and urban development.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201263–65_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201263–65-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> His New Frontier program was strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>'s 1944 "<a href="/wiki/Second_Bill_of_Rights" title="Second Bill of Rights">Second Bill of Rights</a>" address, as well as Harry Truman's <a href="/wiki/Fair_Deal" title="Fair Deal">Fair Deal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200699_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200699-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy also called for a large tax cut as an economic stimulus measure. However, many of his programs were blocked by the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_coalition" title="Conservative coalition">conservative coalition</a> of Republicans and southern Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201263–65_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrinkley201263–65-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The conservative coalition, which controlled key <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_committee" title="United States congressional committee">congressional committees</a> and made up a majority of both houses of Congress during Kennedy's presidency, had prevented the implementation of progressive reforms since the late 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200639_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200639-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's small margin of victory in the 1960 election, his lack of deep connections to influential members of Congress, and his administration's focus on foreign policy also hindered the passage of New Frontier policies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200640–41,_100_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200640–41,_100-142">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Passage of the New Frontier was made even more difficult after the death of Speaker of the House <a href="/wiki/Sam_Rayburn" title="Sam Rayburn">Sam Rayburn</a>; new Speaker <a href="/wiki/John_William_McCormack" class="mw-redirect" title="John William McCormack">John William McCormack</a> and Senate Majority Leader <a href="/wiki/Mike_Mansfield" title="Mike Mansfield">Mike Mansfield</a> both lacked the influence of their predecessors and struggled to exercise effective leadership over committee chairs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006100–101_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006100–101-143">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1961, Kennedy prioritized passing five bills: federal assistance for education, medical insurance for the elderly, housing legislation, federal aid to struggling areas, and an increase in the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States" title="Minimum wage in the United States">federal minimum wage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio200699_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio200699-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's bill to increase the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States" title="Minimum wage in the United States">federal minimum wage</a> to $1.25 an hour passed in early 1961, but an amendment inserted by the staunch segregationist Congressman from Georgia, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Vinson" title="Carl Vinson">Carl Vinson</a>, exempted hundreds of thousands of laundry workers (a job reserved for African-American women at the time) from the law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006102–103_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006102–103-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy also won passage of the Area Redevelopment Act and the Housing Act of 1961. The Area Redevelopment Act provided federal funding to economically struggling regions of the country, while the Housing Act of 1961 provided funds for urban renewal and public housing and authorized federal <a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loans" class="mw-redirect" title="Mortgage loans">mortgage loans</a> to those who did not qualify for public housing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006105–106_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006105–106-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy proposed a bill providing for $2.3 billion in federal educational aid to the states, with more money going to states with lower per-capita income. Though the Senate passed the education bill, it was defeated in the House by a coalition of Republicans, Southern Democrats, and Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006103–104_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006103–104-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Kennedy's health insurance bill, which would have paid for hospitalization and nursing costs for the elderly, failed to pass either house of Congress due to the opposition of Republicans, Southern Democrats, and the <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">American Medical Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006104–105_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006104–105-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> A bill that would have established the Department of Urban Affairs and Housing was also defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006106–107_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006106–107-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1962 and 1963, Kennedy won approval of the Manpower Development and Training Act, designed to provide job retraining, as well as bills that increased the regulation of drug manufacturers and authorized grants and loans for the construction of higher education facilities. Another Kennedy policy, the 1962 Trade Expansion Act, gave the president the power to cut <a href="/wiki/Tariffs_in_United_States_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Tariffs in United States history">tariffs</a> and to take action against countries employing discriminatory tariffs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006107–109_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006107–109-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Following the passage of that act, the U.S. and other countries agreed to major cuts in tariffs in the <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Round" title="Kennedy Round">Kennedy Round</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson2018460–461_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson2018460–461-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Congress also passed the <a href="/wiki/Community_Mental_Health_Act" title="Community Mental Health Act">Community Mental Health Act</a>, providing funding to local mental health community centers. These centers provided out-patient services such as marriage counseling and aid to those suffering from <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996463_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPatterson1996463-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In 1963, Kennedy began to focus more on the issue of poverty, and some of the ideas developed during his presidency would later influence President Johnson's <a href="/wiki/War_on_Poverty" title="War on Poverty">War on Poverty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006119–122_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006119–122-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Peace_Corps">Peace Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Peace Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:JFK_Establishment_of_the_Peace_Corps_edit.ogg" title="File:JFK Establishment of the Peace Corps edit.ogg">Establishment of the Peace Corps</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_4" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="82.337959183673" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="JFK_Establishment_of_the_Peace_Corps_edit.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/JFK_Establishment_of_the_Peace_Corps_edit.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (71 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="71292" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/56/JFK_Establishment_of_the_Peace_Corps_edit.ogg/JFK_Establishment_of_the_Peace_Corps_edit.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="135424" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">John F. Kennedy's announcement of the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a></div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>An agency to enable Americans to volunteer in developing countries appealed to Kennedy because it fit in with his campaign themes of self-sacrifice and volunteerism, while also providing a way to redefine American relations with the Third World.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBernstein1991259-79_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBernstein1991259-79-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Upon taking office, Kennedy issued an executive order establishing the Peace Corps, and he named his brother-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Sargent_Shriver" title="Sargent Shriver">Sargent Shriver</a>, as the agency's first director. Due in large part to Shriver's effective lobbying efforts, Congress approved the permanent establishment of the Peace Corps programs. Kennedy took great pride in the Peace Corps, and he ensured that it remained free of CIA influence, but he largely left its administration to Shriver. In the ensuing twenty-five years, more than 100,000 Americans served in 44 countries as part of the program. Most Peace Corps volunteers taught English in schools, but many became involved in activities like construction and food delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006155–159_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiglio2006155–159-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Presidency_of_John_F._Kennedy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" align="right" style="margin-left:1em; text-align:center">
